文藝三邊吟（偶集譚嗣同句）  白·蕉·　　一騎龍沙道路開，願身成骨骨成灰，邊風冽冽沉悲角，劍帶單于頸血來。　　塡胸狐墳誰堪語，已是共工缺陷天，自向冰天鍊奇骨，馬頭還我好山川。不屈（關外義軍聲勢壯闊敵人疲於奔命）　　不屈男兒在，將軍馬李丁，轉看白日盡，翻愛黑風腥，碧血流金甲，丹心照汗青，平倭問何日，鑄鼎我能銘。科學水産品的製膠法  天·龍·　　前日本刊曼倩君發表的一篇「水産品制膠概說」，他的内容殊佳，實是現在的重要用途。又以普通所用原料，都是利用陸産動物，而對於水産動物中的鱗鏢，皮骨等大都廢棄不用，這是在現今實業漸次發達的時候，不能利用，而專靠舶來品的輸入，是個很可惜的大漏巵丨　　曼倩君對於皮骨鱗鏢水等膠，都是說了一個製造的步序，也可說是一個普遍的大意，因此讀者對於製造方面，恐怕還不甚明瞭，所以作者現在所要討論的，就在這一點。　　皮膠皮膠製造的原料，是凡水産動物的皮，未經單寧鞣製者，多得爲原料，至於他的製造順序，得分左列五項：　　（一）脫毛先拿原料投入石灰水槽中，約浸漬五六日，每日須攪拌二三次，使毛漸次弛緩後，取出放置於脫毛台上，用純刀刮去之（近今亦有用硫酸化鈵炭酸訥及炭酸納和石灰等的混合物以代替石灰乳的）　　（二）膠原料的沸將脫毛後的原料，投入釜中（内須敷設麥桿）加水煑沸，待膠質完全溶解後，乃自下部放出膠液，渣滓即多殘留於釜中的麥桿上。　　（三）膠液的清凈膠的清凈，對於精製上頗有關係。普通都有機械式的清凈桶清凈之。但是這種方法，常不能達到目的，故有用明礬或硫酸鋁等的藥品，以除去蛋白質及膠質分解生成。　　（四）凝固這方法在以前是將清凈後的膠液，蒸發至適當濃度後，即移入凝固箱中凝固之。現在則直接將膠液流注於表面平滑的大石板上，等牠膠化後，切出之。　　（五）乾燥乾燥的方法，我國是採用一種天然乾燥，這一個弊病。歐美各國，則都没有乾燥室（室内裝有蒸氣管，且使日光不能射進而設有通風的裝置）即取切出的膠片，排列在網板上，然後安置接近蒸氣管的棚架上，乾燥之。骨膠骨膠所用的原料，是凡水産動物的骨類，以組織堅密的爲上品，骨呈蜂窠狀的下品，牠的製造順序，得分八項：　　（一）骨的破碎若骨類没有多量的不潔物，可不必水洗，即用碎骨器破碎之。　　（二）脂肪的抽出脂肪的抽出，普通都用揮發性深劑抽之。即用普通的抽出器，在假底下部，敷設蒸氣蛇管，蓋上備有導管，乃將骨類自口中投入，密閉其口，再由溶劑入口處满注溶劑（如四鹽化炭素）通入蒸氣，至溶劑蒸溜告終，乃將蛇管閉塞抽出，而脂肪分即從器底排出。　　（三）浸酸用母氏七八度的稀鹽酸，浸漬脫脂後的骨片，這時鹽酸與骨片中的磷酸石灰相起作用，生出鹽化石灰而磷酸即游離在水溶液中，數日後，骨質便成一種具有彈性的半透明物質。　　（四）膠的抽出膠的抽出，牠的方法很多，歐美各國，都用一種加壓水蒸氣的密閉抽出釜抽出之。即拿浸酸後的原料投入釜中，在最初兩時間，水蒸氣的壓力約十五磅，經過三小時後，减爲五磅，使膠分過蒸氣而溶出，這樣再加温水，膠便充分的抽出了丨　　（五）（六）膠液的澄清漂白和濃縮這手續是與前節所說相同，故不再多說了丨　　（七）凝固用上項方法採製的膠液，應迅速凝固，否則發生腐敗，故經絨布濾過後，即應注入凝固箱中凝固之。　　（八）乾燥將凝固後的膠液，切成適適宜的形狀，放置網板上，於乾燥室中，或空氣流通的地方乾燥之。

1932.09.06

Army Attacks Shenyang Business District, Retreats to Luanshi Mountain After Fierce Battle, Japanese Troops on Qiqihar-Koupai Line Increase Defense of Heilongjiang 1

(Beiping) On the night of the 4th, volunteer armies from Qianjinzai attacked the Shenyang business district along the Hun River. At the same time, volunteer armies were also found at Xiaodongbianmen, Beidaying, and other places. All were small units. After fierce fighting, they retreated towards Luanshi Mountain. Japanese military police have set up electric fences at the radio station, Xiaodongbianmen, Dananbianmen concession, and other places, with heavy security. (5th Dispatch)

(Shanhaiguan) Confirmed reports indicate that most of the volunteer army in the Shenhai Railway area is advancing towards Shenyang from Yingpan. (5th Dispatch)

Volunteer Army Captures Yingpan Station 2

(Beiping) Several hundred volunteer soldiers captured Yingpan Station on the Shenhai Railway on the morning of the 3rd, burning down the station building. Shortly after, a Japanese armored train arrived, leading to a fierce battle. The volunteer army retreated towards Cangshi. The Shenhai Railway remains closed to traffic. (5th Dispatch)

Japanese Army Recaptures Anda Station 3

(Harbin) According to local Russian newspaper reports, the Japanese army has recaptured Anda Station. The Japanese side claims that the volunteer army, which occupied Anda Station several days ago, abandoned 300 dead bodies and retreated. The Japanese side only suffered 4 deaths and 5 injuries. According to another Russian newspaper report, another volunteer army attacked Lukaxifu (transliteration) town, 17 miles east of Yimianpo, and set it on fire. (4th Reuters Dispatch)

Passenger Train Robbed West of Yimianpo 4

(Harbin) Yesterday, a passenger train was attacked by 300 bandits near Wujimi River, 17 miles west of Yimianpo. Passengers' belongings were all robbed. Kuanchengzi is part of the puppet capital, and four volunteer armies are gathered in the nearby area, aiming to attack nearby villages. (4th Reuters Dispatch)

500 Volunteer Soldiers Occupy Yushu 5

(Harbin) According to Japanese sources, 500 anti-Manchukuo soldiers defeated the "Manchukuo" army stationed in Yushu, 33 miles east of Taolai Zhao, and occupied the area. The "Manchukuo" army is currently retreating west. Today, this station received information from Russians that the Red Spear Society has occupied the railway between Ashi River and Yimianpo and is currently clashing with unofficial troops in Erdaohaozi. It is reported that they are trying to seize spheres of influence. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Ma Zhanshan's Former Troops Occupy Qingcheng 6

(Beiping) According to Chinese sources, the volunteer army is engaged in a fierce battle with the Japanese army in Qingcheng. The volunteer army consists of 4,000 soldiers, most of whom are former troops of General Ma Zhanshan. They have occupied the town and are now attacking Suihua. 3,000 Japanese troops are stationed in the area. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Japanese Troops on Qiqihar Line Transferred to Heilongjiang 7

(Beiping) A certain military figure in Heilongjiang province stated that after Ma Zhanshan engaged in a bloody battle with the Japanese army in Dongxingfuyuan in late July, his troops suffered considerable losses. He then transferred all his troops and various brigades, including Wu Songlin's, to the vicinity of Daqing Mountain for reorganization. He also contacted local militias and volunteer armies. Starting on the 23rd of last month, they launched an offensive, pressing against the flanks of the Hu-Hai and Qiqihar lines. Ma himself is commanding from somewhere east of Hailun, with a strength of over 60,000 soldiers. After the Japanese army received news of Ma's counterattack, the Japanese military commander in Heilongjiang, Domon, arranged defenses. He also sent Cheng Zhiyuan, the commander of the Bu Kui Garrison and concurrently the governor of Heilongjiang Province, to Changchun. Han Yunjie, a traitor, has now been appointed as the governor of the province, and Zhang Wengui has been appointed as the commander of the Heilongjiang Garrison, stationed in Zhalantun on the Middle East Line. Zhang Xiange's brigade suddenly hoisted the flag of the Republic of China at the end of last month and renamed his troops the Volunteer Army. The Japanese army, fearing attacks from both sides, urgently transferred the main force from the Qiqihar line back to the provincial capital. Zhang Xiange secretly sent people to contact Ma Zhanshan to find ways to coordinate a counterattack. It is thought that the situation in Heilongjiang Province will develop. (5th Dispatch)

He Zhuguo Returns to Defense from Beidaihe 8

(Beiping) A person from Yuguan stated that Yuguan is peaceful. He Zhuguo has returned to defense from Beidaihe and personally leads troops to patrol every night. A curfew is imposed every night at 10 PM. Japanese planes still circle Yuguan from time to time. The puppet Fengshan Railway train arrives on time recently. (5th Dispatch)

Investigation Team's Report Conclusion Not Yet Drafted, German and French Members Depart for Dalian from Tanggu 9

(Beiping) Lytton telegraphed to Peiping, expressing his gratitude for the hospitality. (5th Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received news that the Lytton Investigation Team's report seemed more moderate than previously reported, and it was rumored that the conclusion had not yet been drafted. Therefore, no statement was submitted to the League of Nations, only mentioning that the developments in the situation between the drafting of the report and its receipt in Geneva should be taken into consideration. A spokesperson for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs commented on the report, saying that there was one important point that Japan must clarify: if the League of Nations investigation team could not reach a conclusion after half a year of thorough investigation, then how could a place as far away as Geneva be considered capable of making a fair judgment? (5th Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) Liu Difan, who was sent by the reception office to escort the investigation team, returned to Peiping this afternoon and said that the German and French members departed from Tanggu on the Changping Maru at 2:30 this morning, heading for Dalian. (5th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways will send the English report and pictures of the losses suffered by the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways during the Shanghai Incident to Yan Deqing, a special commissioner of the Chinese delegation attending the League of Nations Assembly, for forwarding to the investigation team for reference. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) The plane that sent Lytton and Ford returned to Peiping this afternoon. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) The investigation team's report was prepared in four copies. Each member formally signed two copies, and the land and sea groups each took one copy to Geneva. The remaining two copies are currently in the hands of Haas, the secretary-general who came to Peiping, and will be shown to the Chinese and Japanese governments before the main text is published in Geneva. At that time, secretariat members will be sent from Peiping to Nanjing and Tokyo. (5th Telegraphic Communication Agency Dispatch)

Puppet State's Negotiations with Russia Regarding Border Russian Military Activities 10

(Harbin) The Soviet Union previously responded to the "Manchukuo" authorities, saying that there was absolutely no basis for the claim that the Soviet Union was building barracks and trenches near the Manchurian border and that Russian soldiers were appearing in Chinese territory. The "Manchukuo" government regards this text as unsatisfactory. Since the opinions of the two sides differ, the recent negotiations have reached a stalemate. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Peiping Military Council Discusses Internal Organization, Three Departments Have Been Reorganized 11

(Beiping) The Peiping Military Council held a meeting this morning to discuss internal organization issues. Rong Wan and others reorganized the various departments and sections of the old Suiyuan Supervisory Office in accordance with the organizational regulations. It is reported that the Military Affairs, Military Orders, and General Affairs departments have been reorganized. Bao Yue, Wang Shuhan, and Zhu Guangmu will serve as the heads of the three departments. The heads of each group are still being selected. The entire organization will be decided after another meeting. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Peiping Political Affairs Committee will hold a routine meeting tomorrow morning. Zhang Xueliang plans to attend in person to discuss (1) the case of the Palace Museum stealing and selling metal objects and (2) the case of personnel changes in the Hebei-Chahar Provincial Government Affairs Office. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Peiping Federation of Trade Unions requests the Military Council to send troops out of the Pass before September 18th to suppress the rebels. (5th Dispatch)

Yan Xishan's Expression to Zhang Qun, Extremely Willing to Assist the Central Government and Jointly Take Responsibility 12

(Taiyuan) After Zhang Qun arrived in Bing on the evening of the 4th, Yan visited him twice and talked for a long time. Yan also hosted a banquet for Zhang to wash away the dust. Xu Yongchang and military and political figures publicly hosted a banquet for Zhang Qun, Zhao Daiwen, Zhao Pilian, Fu Zuoyi, etc. at noon on the 5th, and a dinner was planned for Zhang in the evening. Zhang told reporters that he came to Bing to visit Yan to renew old friendships and exchange opinions on the current situation. After returning south, he will report to the Central Government and Chiang. Yan expressed his extreme willingness to assist the Central Government and Chiang, jointly take responsibility, and carry out national affairs. It was also discussed that Zhang Xueliang plans to go to Wuhan soon to meet Chiang. Zhang is scheduled to meet with Yan again on the 6th and leave Bing for Wuhan on the 20th to report to Chiang. (5th Dispatch)

Dalai Lama Decides to Recruit Militia to Counterattack Ganzi and Zhanhua 13

(Beiping) Lanzhou Telegram: The Dalai Lama has decided to recruit militia to counterattack from Qamdo. Newly purchased military equipment is being transported into Kham in large quantities. Four airplanes are practicing in Lhasa and will depart with the Dalai Lama. It is planned to take advantage of the cold weather to regain the lost territory of Ganzi and Zhanhua. Hainan has switched to a defensive posture, and the situation is relatively relaxed. (5th Dispatch)

Eurasia Flight No. 5 Scheduled to Continue to Suzhou 14

(Beiping) Lanzhou Telegram: Eurasia Flight No. 5 is scheduled to continue to Suzhou on the 8th. Flights No. 1 and 6 will not return to Peiping for the time being and will be dedicated to flights in the Northwest. It is too cold in Tacheng for test flights. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Today, this station received a telegram from Chinese sources in Xi'an stating that Eurasia Aviation's planes had two accidents in Gansu Province. Flight No. 1 crashed in Yongchang while test flying from Lanzhou to Suzhou and was destroyed. The German pilot and one Chinese passenger were injured and are now being treated in a Lanzhou hospital. Flight No. 6, which traveled between Lanzhou and the capital, crashed into a mountain. Two female passengers, both relatives of Chairman Shao, suffered minor injuries. It is now rumored that Eurasia Aviation has decided to suspend passenger aviation services on that route. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Song Ziwen Plans North China Financial Plan 15

(Nanjing) Financial Commissioner Jing Youyan, carrying Zhang Xueliang's mandate to negotiate financial issues in North China, arrived in Shanghai on the afternoon of the 5th after arriving in Nanjing to visit Finance Minister Song and discuss everything. It is understood that Song has an entire plan for cleaning up North China's finances, which will combine the revenues of the four provinces of Hebei, Suiyuan, Chahar, and Rehe and Tianjin and use them for military and administrative expenses in North China. If there is a shortfall, the central government will find ways to remedy it. (5th Dispatch)

Japan's Reply to the Japanese Postal Correspondence, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Plans to Refute 16

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of Japanese residents setting up post offices in Shanghai, Qingdao, Tianjin, and other places, after the Ministry of Foreign Affairs lodged a serious protest with Japan, it received a reply from the Japanese side, citing the convenience of communication for Japanese residents and stating that there was no violation of the law. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has decided to use the Japanese side's reply, pointing out that the wording is vague and intends to deceive. It has been decided that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will refute it point by point based on the facts and will be issued within days. (5th Dispatch)

Ministry of Communications Telegraphed to the Southwest Political Council to Cancel Telegraph Surcharges 17

(Nanjing) The Southwest Political Affairs Committee recently increased telegram charges in the Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, and Yunnan regions. Guangdong and Guangxi provinces have already implemented it. The Ministry of Communications believes that this move disrupts the administrative system and undermines the consistent rules of the whole country. In addition to telegrahing the Guangdong and Guangxi Telecommunications Administration to cancel the surcharge by a set date, it also telegraphed the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, asking it to withdraw its order and stop the surcharge method immediately. In addition, the Hong Kong Special Region Telecommunications Administration telegraphed the Ministry of Communications to request instructions after receiving the surcharge order from the Southwest Political Affairs Committee. The Ministry of Communications also replied yesterday by telegram, disallowing the implementation. (5th Dispatch)

Jiang Guangnai Has Agreed to Become Chairman of Fujian 18

(Nanjing) It is rumored that Jiang Guangnai has expressed his willingness to become the chairman of the Fujian Provincial Government. The candidates for department directors have also been internally decided, with Deng Yuanxun as the Director of the Civil Affairs Department and Fan Qiwu as the Director of the Finance Department. (5th Dispatch)

Chairman Chiang's Speech at Headquarters 19

(Hankou) On the morning of the 5th, the Bandit Suppression Headquarters held a weekly memorial service for the Premier in the headquarters auditorium. Over a hundred officers and staff from various departments attended. After General Commander Chiang led the ceremony, he gave a speech, encouraging the staff to value their time and pay attention to the effectiveness of their work. He also said that in the progress of the bandit suppression military operations, political affairs personnel sometimes failed to keep up with the army, so the political work that urgently needed to be carried out could not be started immediately. Bandit suppression requires seven parts political power. This phenomenon, where political facilities cannot keep up with military progress, must be improved. He hoped that political and military affairs would advance simultaneously in the future to achieve complete success in bandit suppression. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Remaining Bandits in Honghu Can Be Eliminated in the Short Term, Xu Yuanquan Flew to Yuekou Today to Continue Suppression 20

(Hankou) He Chengjun and Xu Yuanquan visited Chairman Chiang at the headquarters on the morning of the 5th after the weekly memorial service to report on the latest progress in bandit suppression in the central Hubei region. After leaving, Xu visited Zhang Nanxian to discuss post-disaster relief in Mianyang. It was decided that he would fly back to Yuekou and then to the front line by plane on the morning of the 6th to continue suppressing the remaining bandits in Honghu. Xu Yuanquan told reporters that the central Hubei region had undergone repeated fierce battles. The Red bandits' pseudo-Seventh Division had been completely eliminated, and most of the pseudo-Eighth Division had been annihilated. Many bandit chiefs and regimental and company commanders had been captured successively and would be sent to Hankou within days for disposal by the headquarters. Currently, Qujiawan and Liujiaji have been occupied by our troops, and the remaining bandits are gathering in Honghu. We are currently pressing forward step by step, and it is certain that they can be eliminated in the shortest possible time. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Headquarters Announces Administrative Inspector Commissioners 21

(Hankou) Headquarters announced the administrative inspector commissioners for the five districts on the 5th: Tang Ken for the second district, Shi Yuling for the third district, Cheng Ruhhuai for the fourth district, Yu Dianshu for the sixth district, and Lei Xiaocen for the seventh district. The rest will be announced within days. (5th Dispatch)

Jiang Dingwen Visited Chiang Yesterday, Reported on the Security Situation on the Jinpu Railway 22

(Hankou) Jiang Dingwen visited Chiang on the 5th to report on the security situation on the Jinpu Railway and the handling of the Lingbi-Suxian civil unrest. Chiang instructed that corrupt local tyrants must be severely punished, and the masses must be organized to strictly prevent Communist bandits from inciting them. Chiang is scheduled to return to defense on the 7th. (5th Dispatch)

Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi Send Troops to Encircle and Suppress the Kong Bandits 23

(Hankou) The joint suppression of the Kong bandits by troops from Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi is about to begin. Hunan will send one division, Jiangxi will send three divisions, and they will join forces with the Hubei army to carry out a large-scale encirclement. (5th Dispatch)

Mao's Division Recovers Nanfeng, Zhu, Mao, and Peng Bandits Have Retreated to Guangchang 24

(Nanchang) The bandits from Yihuang and Nanfeng jointly attacked Nancheng, but were severely defeated by our forces, with countless bandits killed. Taking advantage of the victory, Mao's division pursued them past Xinfeng Street and captured Nanfeng City on the 3rd. Zhu, Mao, and Peng's pseudo-First, Third, and Fifth Army Corps have retreated to Guangchang. It is reported that the Fujian army has captured Huichang. (5th Dispatch)

Xiao and Hu Discuss Proposals for the Third Plenary Session 25

(Hong Kong) Xiao Focheng has extended his leave from the Southwest Political Affairs Committee for another month. The Southwest has decided to act in concert with the Shanghai Committee on the proposals for the Third Plenary Session. Xiao came to Hong Kong to discuss this matter with Hu. Huang and Bai are scheduled to come to Hong Kong from Guilin on the 2nd and 3rd to meet with Hu and Xiao. The newspapers of the Wang clique have been advocating the convening of a National Political Participation Council with great effort in recent days, under Wang's orders. (5th Dispatch)

Anti-Japanese Movement in Guangzhou 26

(Guangzhou) Due to the developments in Shanghai, anti-Japanese sentiments are becoming increasingly intense here. The disciplinary squads have resumed their activities in recent days, so Japanese goods have completely disappeared from the market. Today, the Student Union decided to carry out an anti-Japanese movement on September 18th. Various theaters will also perform patriotic dramas on that day to arouse the enthusiasm of the people. The Student Union will also petition the authorities to execute a certain representative of the National Salvation Association who was detained for receiving bribes from those who privately transport Japanese goods. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Gu Zhutong Denies Opium Public Sales in Jiangsu Province 27

(Zhenjiang) At the provincial government's weekly memorial service on the 5th, Chairman Gu Zhutong reported on the administration in August and said that all administrative affairs of this government are open and there are absolutely no secrets. The rumors that opium is being sold publicly are completely unfounded. Whether it is well-intentioned correction or malicious attack, it is not worth refuting. If you want to ask whether Jiangsu Province is selling opium publicly, just ask whether the central government has promulgated laws and regulations regarding the public sale of opium in Jiangsu Province and whether Jiangsu Province has formulated its own regulations regarding the public sale of opium. Since it is called public sale, there must be an organization to promulgate laws and regulations. Since there are no such laws and regulations now, it can be proven that the rumors that Jiangsu Province is selling opium publicly are absolutely untrue. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Standing Committee's Discussion Meeting Adjourned Yesterday 28

(Nanjing) The Standing Committee's discussion meeting on the 5th was adjourned because only one standing committee member, Chen Guofu, was present, and the number of attendees was also small. (5th Dispatch)

Mongolian Committee Prepares for Tibetan-Mongolian School 29

(Nanjing) The Mongolian Committee has appointed Ke Xing'e, Li Peitian, and others to prepare for the establishment of a Tibetan-Mongolian school. A preparatory office has been established and work has begun. (5th Dispatch)

Capital Ferry Scheduled to Launch 30

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways' capital ferryboat is scheduled to hold a launching ceremony on October 1st. The ship names have also been determined to be Changjiang and Tianjin. (5th Dispatch)

Shashi Post Office Collects Bandit Suppression Tax 31

(Nanjing) The Hubei Postal Administration submitted a report to the Ministry of Communications stating that the Upper Yangtze Bandit Suppression Headquarters has set up a counter at the Shashi Post Office to collect bandit suppression taxes, which hinders postal services. It is requested that measures be taken to stop it. It is said that the new and old Public Security Bureau directors did not hand over yesterday. The problem of police salaries arose. According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Mr. Wen Yingxing, director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, resigned due to the theft of soil in the bureau. The municipal government approved the resignation and appointed Mr. Wen Hongen to succeed him. The handover was originally scheduled for yesterday morning, but due to the monthly accumulation of arrears in police salaries, etc., no arrangements had been made, so the handover could not be completed. The conversation of Mr. Wen is recorded as follows: According to Mr. Wen's statement to the reporter of Xin Sheng News Agency, the reason why the handover could not be completed today was entirely due to the accumulation of more than 100,000 yuan in police salaries. The expenses for August were used to cover the police salaries for July, and the police salaries for August were still unsettled. The reason for this was that after the January 28th War in this city, the expenses of various agencies were greatly reduced. The expenses of the Public Security Bureau were cut to 120,000 yuan, while the actual expenses increased due to the following reasons: (1) The police training school of this bureau was dismantled after the Shanghai War. At that time, it was a pity to put so many well-trained students into idleness, and it was even more worrying to add so many unemployed people to the society. Moreover, the bureau also felt that the police force was weak. Therefore, it was reported to Mayor Wu for approval to select and organize seven police teams (four teams were assigned to the Security Office). The start-up expenses have not yet been allocated by the Finance Bureau, and the monthly salaries have not been increased. (2) When the fourth, fifth, and seventh districts that had fallen into the war zone were not taken over, the district chiefs who were transferred to the bureau only received a monthly salary of 50 yuan. After the takeover in May, the old appearance was restored, and each district added a translator, but the expenses have not been increased. (3) The production of household registration plates and licenses was reported to the Municipal Government in March, and merchants were recruited to undertake the production, which cost more than 10,000 yuan. The municipal government has not asked about it for a long time, and the contractors will certainly not agree to take it back. The above three items amount to more than 120,000 yuan. I do not have the financial resources to advance such a huge amount of money, so I used it month by month, which led to the transfer of the expenses for August to cover the police salaries for July. Therefore, I cannot hand over the accounts until a solution is found. Otherwise, if the expenses for August have been issued but the police salaries have not been issued, wouldn't it become Shanghai's so-called "mess"? Regarding the handover time, at 3:30 p.m., the municipal government called Director Wen Yingxing to inquire when the handover could be completed. Mr. Wen replied that all procedures had been completed, and the handover could be completed within 30 minutes after the municipal government approved the above three items of expenses and received the official documents. After Mayor Wu Tiecheng approved Wen Yingxing's resignation, he planned to appoint Mr. Wen as a commissioner of the Municipal Government. However, Mr. Wen said that this time he resigned for dereliction of duty, and it was already a fluke that the Municipal Government did not punish him. It would be difficult to take on the position of commissioner again, so as to increase his guilt. According to the China East News Agency, after Mr. Wen's resignation was approved, important officials of the bureau, such as Zhen Shao, chief of the first section, Wang Zhijing, chief of the second section, Wu Zhiquan, chief of the third section, Gong Xikui, chief inspector, Zhang Mengjia and Feng Yuanxiang, secretaries, and Wang Dian, chief of the first district, Chen Dongkai, chief of the second district, and He Yiming, chief of the fifth district, all submitted their resignations. Various trade associations organized a committee to uphold the League of Nations Covenant and implement economic sanctions based on the League of Nations Charter. The Shanghai Municipal Mining Ash Industry, Silk and Satin Industry, Cotton Cloth Industry, North-South Goods Exchange Industry, Sugar Industry, Flying Flower Industry, Mercerized Cotton Weaving Industry, Rice Store Industry, Sausage Industry, Color Printing Industry, Sales of Lime Industry, Woolen Industry, New Medicine Industry, Coal Industry, and more than seventy other trade associations, believing that Japan had occupied our Northeast since September 18 and attacked Shanghai in January 28, disregarding the League of Nations Covenant and engaging in wanton aggression. Recently, it has intensified and wants to interfere with the patriotic movement of our people. Therefore, based on the principle of free trade for merchants and civilians, they organized a committee to uphold the League of Nations Covenant and implement economic sanctions against Japan in accordance with Article 16 of the Covenant. The declaration is recorded as follows: China is a country that loves peace and respects the opinions of the League of Nations. This spirit was conceived in the Confucian ideology more than 4,000 years ago and was evident after the September 18th Incident. The Chinese government and its entire people have adopted a tolerant attitude. Because they love peace, they must prevent the spread and expansion of seeds that disturb world peace through peaceful struggle. Because they respect the opinions of the League of Nations, they will not allow any slightest deviation from the League of Nations Covenant, the greatest international authority, and vow to take the lead in implementing it. Since the September 18th Incident, the suffering that China has suffered from the Japanese can be said to be unparalleled. If we want to force a comparison with appropriate words and sentences, we can only say, "If any European country with a territory smaller than China were in this situation, the entire country would have been destroyed long ago." However, China knows that the League of Nations' resolutions are complicated and time-consuming, which will invisibly increase Japan's attempts to take advantage of the situation. Still, it has adopted an attitude of trust in everything. Why? Because justice is on our side, we firmly believe that the League of Nations was established to uphold international justice. China has always stood on the side of justice and will certainly receive just treatment, so it is open and without suspicion. Japan's cowardly attitude is the opposite of China's. It says that if the report is not beneficial to it, Japan will do this and that. Even before the report of the International Investigation Team has been released, it openly recognizes the false organizations it has created and further concludes a treaty of alliance. In short, Japan does not recognize the existence of the League of Nations authority from beginning to end. The so-called Asian Monroe Doctrine is a diplomatic term that denies the League of Nations and replaces it with war. China, as a country that has suffered from its poison, has the right to demand that the League of Nations apply Article 16 of the Covenant, and even has the obligation to implement it itself first. The question that is generally raised at present is whether Chinese citizens can invoke this Covenant and suddenly implement this economic blockade before the League of Nations decides to implement Article 16 of the Covenant. The committee believes that the blockade in Article 16 of the Covenant originates from the resolution of the League of Nations and is emphasized by the government's orders. The people's voluntary economic blockade, although its principle is already included in Article 16 of the Covenant, its origin is based on the principle of free trade for the people. Therefore, the procedure for implementing the blockade does not have to be launched at the same time as the government's orders and the League of Nations' resolutions. Why? Before the government decides to blockade the country through the League of Nations, it has the treaty obligations that allow it to trade. However, we should first understand the following points: (1) The Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce and Navigation has long expired and has not been renewed. Therefore, strictly speaking, it has already entered a state of no treaty. (2) Even if we reluctantly recognize that the expired treaty has been abolished, the fact is that it has not been abolished. The government still has the obligation to maintain the treaty. However, according to Article 7 of the treaty, the government only has the obligation not to prohibit the employment of Chinese people to handle legitimate affairs. According to Article 9, the government only has the obligation to allow the free transportation of goods that are not restricted or prohibited from import in the laws and regulations of China and Western countries. In short, the government only has the obligation not to prohibit transportation, but it has no obligation to order or persuade merchants to guarantee sales or people to purchase. Therefore, merchants who organize alliances to refuse to sell goods from a certain country are not subject to the treaty or laws before the government implements the economic blockade procedures. To take another example, after the Mukden Incident, Japan unanimously refused to buy alkali from the Yongli Company in Tianjin, China. Why did the international community act as if nothing had happened and no one criticized it? It is also because merchants and civilians have the right to organize groups and freely decide whether to refuse or not. In order to uphold the spirit of the League of Nations Covenant and strive for peace, and based on the principle of free trade for the people, we hereby initiate this association with the purpose of merchants' self-determination through the trade associations of various industries in the commercial group. We will automatically implement economic sanctions against ambitious countries that destroy the League of Nations Charter and invade our country's territory. We will not be afraid of violence, we will not be coerced, and we will do our best until we die. We hope that all compatriots in the country will rise up and plan together. This is our declaration. The left and right nearby Sima returned to Shanghai to report on the recent situation of foreign warships in Shanghai. There were no inspection activities by Japanese warships in Shanghai. Recently, there have been rumors that Japanese warships have been concentrated in Shanghai for inspection, and some have said that 19 Japanese warships have arrived in Shanghai and are anchored in the Huangpu River. After detailed investigation by our newspaper reporters, the rumor of Japanese warships gathering in Shanghai is purely a rumor, and there are only seven Japanese warships anchored in the Huangpu River. Including the foreign warships of the five countries, including Britain, the United States, Italy, France, and Japan, there are also less than 19 ships. Yesterday, Zuo Jinsi had already come to Shanghai, and today there is no plan to go to Wusong to inspect the Japanese warship exercises at the outer school. The details are recorded as follows: Izumo returned to Shanghai. The Japanese navy in the Yangtze River originally belonged to the First Foreign Dispatch Team. Since the January 28th War, the Japanese Naval Ministry has increased the dispatch of the 15th and 24th Destroyer Teams with eight destroyers to Shanghai, and then added the Third Fleet, ordering the ships of the First and Second Foreign Dispatch Teams to control the Yangtze River and Qingdao. This time, Zuo Jinsi went to Hankou to inspect the ships of the First Foreign Dispatch Team. On the second day of this month, after the matter was completed, he went east. The flagship Izumo did not stop in Nanjing when passing by, and immediately sailed to Shanghai. The light cruiser Tokiwa, which was transferred to Shanghai during the Shanghai War to participate in the attack on Wusong, has been stationed in Shanghai for seven months. It has now been ordered to withdraw and return to Sasebo to join the team. The Tokiwa was originally berthed at buoys No. 7 and 8 in the Huangpu River. Yesterday, after the captain met with Zuo Jinsi, it was decided to set sail from the Osaka Wharf in Yangshupu at 9:00 a.m. tomorrow to return home. It is heard that after the ship returns to Japan, it will be incorporated into the training fleet. Japanese warships in the Huangpu River. The number of Japanese warships currently stationed in Shanghai is usually no more than five or six. There are 12 ships belonging to the First Foreign Dispatch Team stationed in the Yangtze River, and there are also two torpedo boat teams. However, one is stationed in various locations upstream and downstream, and the other is mobile and patrolling outside. According to yesterday's investigation, there are only (1) the Yangtze River flagship Ataka, anchored at the Japanese Navy River Pier, (2) the Jiangfang ship Katata, anchored at river piers B7 and 8, (3) the cruiser Tenryu, anchored at river piers 9 and 10, (4) the gunboat Toba, anchored on the Jiangmian River in Yangshupu, (5) the gunboat CaAtmi, anchored at river piers B9 and 10, and (6) a torpedo of the 15th team, anchored at the Mitsui Wharf. Including Izumo, there are only seven ships. Foreign warships stationed in Shanghai. Today, Zuo Jinsi did not go to the Huangpu River or Wusong to inspect the Japanese warships, because there are not many Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai. As for the foreign warships of Britain, the United States, Italy, and France in Shanghai, there are a total of nine ships. The details are recorded as follows: (1) The French gunboat Argus, anchored on the Waiyangjing Jiangmian River; (2) The gunboat Balapo in front of the Jiangnan Shipyard; (3) The French flagship Manpian, anchored at river pier C1; (4) The American gunboat Chim, anchored in front of the Dalai Wharf; (5) The American cruiser Rochester, anchored at the river pier on the Jiangmian River in the French Concession; (6) The gunboat Sacramento, anchored at the Meifu Wharf; (7) The Italian destroyer Esplo, anchored at river piers B1 and 2; (8) The British gunboat Kilby, anchored at the Huatong Wharf in Pudong; (9) The Jiangfang ship Mendes, anchored at the Lanyancong Wharf. Northwest Airlines Exhibition Postponed. The official maiden voyage will be around the 20th of this month. The Beijing-Shanghai route will resume its original flight today. Eurasia Airlines sent personnel from Peiping on the 10th of last month to fly the entire route for trial flights, and arranged stations along the way for trial flights. The trial plane has arrived in Dihua, and after flying to Tacheng immediately, it can fly directly back to Shanghai from its destination. The company has also set the flight times and prices for the autumn and winter seasons of this year and is preparing for the official maiden voyage. Intermodal transportation between Europe and Asia has also been negotiated. The Beijing-Shanghai line will also be restored to its original flight starting today. The reporter of China East News Agency interviewed the company's secretary, Mr. Sun Mutang, yesterday, and received a detailed report. The details are recorded as follows: Official maiden voyage date. The company sent the director of the Operations Group, Liao Guanxuan, and the director of the Shipping Group, Shi Mite, to depart from Peiping on the newly arrived Eurasia No. 6 aircraft driven by Captain Lusi, and it was originally scheduled to complete the entire route back to Shanghai on the 25th of this month. Later, due to the time required to arrange stations along the way, and because the trial flight crashed suddenly near Lanzhou on the 26th, it was not possible to return to Shanghai according to the scheduled schedule. However, it continued to be sent to the west the next day. According to Secretary Sun, the plane arrived in Dihua the day before yesterday and is currently test-flying Tacheng. After arriving in Tacheng, it will fly directly back to Shanghai on a certain day. It is expected that it will arrive in Shanghai around the 10th. If the gasoline supply in Hami Dihua Tacheng, etc. is sufficient and convenient, and no problems occur at the stations, it can officially open to traffic on the 15th. Otherwise, it will be able to open to traffic around the 20th. After implementation, there will be one round trip flight per week. Flight fields at each station. The flight fields at each station along the Shanghai-Tacheng route and the offices in various places will be decided after the test flight returns to Shanghai, except for a part that is still to be decided. Those that have been completed include the Shanghai flight field in Hongqiao and the office on the third floor of No. 25 Renji Road; the Peiping flight field in Nanyuan and the office at No. 88 Beichizi; the Nanjing flight field in Ming Palace and the office at No. 12 Liangyou Lane, Sishitiao Lane; the Luoyang flight field in Xigong and the office also in Xigong; the Xi'an flight field in the western suburbs and the office also in the same place; the Lanzhou flight field in the eastern suburbs and the office also in the same place. The rest, such as Suzhou, Hami, Dihua, and Tacheng, will be decided after the trial flight returns to Shanghai. Autumn and winter schedule. The schedule set by the company is only applicable to the autumn and winter seasons of this year. The schedule will be changed at any time thereafter without notice. There is one round trip per week. The westward flight departs from Shanghai every Tuesday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Nanjing at 9:00 a.m., departs from Nanjing at 9:30 a.m., arrives in Luoyang at 2:00 p.m. on the same day, departs from Luoyang at 2:30 p.m., and arrives in Xi'an at 4:30 p.m. The westward flight departs from Xi'an every Wednesday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Lanzhou at 10:45 a.m., departs from Lanzhou at 11:45 a.m., and arrives in Suzhou at 4:00 p.m. on the same day. The westward flight departs from Suzhou every Thursday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Hami at 10:45 a.m., departs from Hami at 11:45 a.m., and arrives in Dihua at 3:00 p.m. on the same day. On Friday, departs from Dihua at 7:00 a.m. and arrives in Tacheng at 10:30 a.m. The westward flight departing from Peiping departs from Peiping every Tuesday at 8:00 a.m. and arrives in Luoyang at 12:30 p.m. The route from Luoyang to Tacheng is the same as the schedule for the plane departing from Shanghai. The eastbound flight departs from Tacheng every Tuesday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Dihua at 10:30 a.m., departs from Dihua at 11:20 a.m., and arrives in Hami at 2:45 p.m. on the same day. The eastbound flight departs from Hami every Wednesday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Suzhou at 10:45 a.m., departs from Suzhou at 11:45 a.m., and arrives in Lanzhou at 4:00 p.m. on the same day. The eastbound flight departs from Lanzhou every Thursday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Xi'an at 10:45 a.m., departs from Xi'an at 11:45 a.m., and arrives in Luoyang at 1:45 p.m. on the same day. The eastbound flight departs from Luoyang every Friday at 7:00 a.m., arrives in Nanjing at 11:30 a.m., departs from Nanjing at 12:00 p.m., and arrives in Shanghai at 2:00 p.m. on the same day. The plane arriving in Peiping departs from Luoyang at 7:00 a.m. on Friday and arrives in Peiping at 11:30 a.m. Passenger fare list. The full fare from Shanghai to Tacheng is 5,555 yuan, including 50 yuan from Shanghai to Nanjing, 100 yuan from Nanjing or Peiping to Luoyang, 75 yuan from Luoyang to Xi'an, 230 yuan from Xi'an to Lanzhou, 300 yuan from Lanzhou to Suzhou, 275 yuan from Suzhou to Hami, 250 yuan from Hami to Dihua, and 275 yuan from Dihua to Tacheng. The above fares are calculated in national currency. Passengers are allowed to carry 10 kilograms of free luggage. For luggage exceeding the quota, a fee of 1.5% of the ticket price will be charged per kilogram. Distance in kilometers. The total length of the route is 4,050 kilometers, including 270 kilometers from Shanghai to Nanjing, 690 kilometers from Nanjing to Luoyang, 320 kilometers from Luoyang to Xi'an, 570 kilometers from Xi'an to Lanzhou, 625 kilometers from Lanzhou to Suzhou, 550 kilometers from Suzhou to Hami, 500 kilometers from Hami to Dihua, and 525 kilometers from Dihua to Tacheng. Intermodal transportation between Europe and Asia. The issue of intermodal transportation between Europe and Asia is very important. Since our country closed the Northeast Post Office, the mail that was originally transferred to Europe via the Siberian Railway has been reloaded onto ships and taken to Europe by sea, which has been delayed and is very inconvenient. Therefore, Director of Posts Lin Shi has consulted with Eurasia Airlines several times, intending to have the company find a way to transport mail by plane in order to resist the obstruction of postal rights. This matter has been concluded. According to Mr. Sun, the intermodal transportation between Europe and Asia has been negotiated and the intermodal postal method has been agreed upon. After the official maiden voyage, the post office will telegraph the International Postal Union to inform the post offices of various countries to collect and send Eurasian airmail. Resumption of Beijing-Shanghai line. The Beijing-Shanghai line from Shanghai to Nanjing was temporarily suspended due to the impact of the war. The company believes that it is extremely inconvenient for passengers on the Beijing-Shanghai line recently, and the mail in various ports has not been smooth. Therefore, it has been decided to resume operations starting today.

Tanzi Bay robbery and shooting. The police bravely fought and almost captured all the bandits alive. A truck suddenly came and the thieves covered their escape. Yesterday morning, a robbery and injury case occurred in Xiaoshadu, Tanzi Bay, Zhabei. Three robbers robbed the home of Wang Xueyou, a resident of the area. After obtaining the stolen goods, they fled west to the railway line along Tanzi Bay. They happened to meet the patrol police there and fought each other. The bandits were no match and fled over the canal. The police pursued closely and were about to capture them alive when a Shanghai-Hangzhou night freight train suddenly passed by, blocking their pursuit. The three robbers robbed. At 1:30 am yesterday morning, three robbers wearing blue cloth short shirts and trousers suddenly came to the teahouse shop of Wang Xueyou (31 years old), a native of Yancheng, located at No. 86 Xiaoshadu, behind the Fuxin Flour Mill in Tanzi Bay. Two robbers were on the lookout outside, and one robber went straight into Wang's bedroom, pulled out a pistol, and forced him to hand over silver coins. Wang was intimidated by the threat and handed over the keys. The robber searched wantonly and robbed 48 yuan in silver dollars and 10 jiao in small coins, and then fled out the door. The shopkeeper was shot and killed. Wang was a small business operator. His wife, Chen, witnessed the robbers robbing all of his savings and leaving. She was filled with resentment and shouted, "Catch the robbers!" The robbers were frightened and turned back to Wang and fired three shots in succession. Two shots hit Wang's head, entering from the right temple and exiting from the back of the head. One shot entered the left arm, and Wang fell to the ground and died on the spot. The robbers fled along the railway line. Firing guns to resist the police. The wires in the Tanzi Bay Jinghu Railway area had been stolen many times before, so recently the authorities specially sent police officers to guard the area. At 11:00 pm the night before, Inspector Xu Jintang of the Fourth District Police Station led Police Chief Zhang Linqing, police officers Zhao Xinzhou, Qi Wenxian, etc., and were patrolling along the railway near the Central Mint. Suddenly, they saw three people gathering in a corner in the darkness in front of them, whispering to each other. Inspector Zhang observed their situation and suspected that they were not good people, probably the three robbers mentioned above. The police stepped forward and ordered them to stand up. Unexpectedly, one of the robbers suddenly fired a gun to resist the police. Inspector Wang ordered them to return fire. The two sides fought, firing more than a dozen shots. The robbers were no match and tried to escape by crossing the canal behind them. The police chased desperately and were only a few steps away when more than a dozen trains suddenly sped by, blocking their pursuit. Moreover, the area was extremely dark and they could not distinguish east from west. By the time the trains passed, the robbers had already escaped into the territory of the Sixth District. A woman cried at night. The police saw that the robbers had fled far away and were still afraid that the remnants were hiding nearby, so they searched the surrounding area. Suddenly, they heard a woman crying. They stepped forward to check and saw the woman holding her husband's body and sobbing. After inquiring, they learned the details and immediately reported to the Fourth District Headquarters. Gold Price Continues to Decline

The market state is erratic. Yesterday, the gold price continued to decline. The market was volatile and unpredictable, with fluctuations of over five taels in both the morning and afternoon sessions. The chaotic situation was uncontrollable, with a final drop of over two taels. The public sentiment remained uncertain, and the demand from various parties varied greatly. The opening price broke the 700 tael mark, likely due to the rise in silver prices yesterday. Subsequent ups and downs were constant. Active buying was driven by the Central Bank's aggressive purchase of 840 bars of spot gold at prices ranging from 703 to 704 taels, sold by companies like Dade Cheng and Heng Xing to hedge futures positions. This boosted the market and pushed prices above 700 taels. However, the trend in drafts was loose and excessive, seemingly contradictory. The afternoon market felt even weaker, and sellers became active, pushing prices back below 700 taels. Today (6th) is a holiday in the United States, so there is no silver market. The overall situation was slightly calmer, and the market sentiment was slightly stable, with some people taking advantage of the low prices to buy in, but major players were waiting and not moving. The market sentiment among buyers and sellers was very even. Although prices rebounded, the fluctuations were very small. The result was about half a yuan better than last week.

The cotton yarn market is weakening, and the situation is very weak. The loose cotton and the soft sentiment have led sellers to take the opportunity to become active, and the market is becoming increasingly weak. The majority of psychology is that domestic demand is not smooth, and the idea of selling is stronger. Only Rongxing continues to maintain a quiet attitude.

Cotton Plummeted Violently

Plummeted More Than One Tael

The cotton market plummeted, and the decline was very sharp. The Ningbo gang vigorously dumped about 40,000 dan in the morning market. The reason for this was that new cotton was launched on the market, and the inland shipments were surging, and sales were relatively sluggish. Therefore, they were sold in Shanghai. The market fell sharply by more than one tael (it was found that Zhejiang province produced more than 490,000 dan of cotton throughout the year). However, the American and Indian cotton markets were still rising, so Japanese merchants were gradually inquiring about Chinese cotton.

This kind of fall is rare in history. The far month fell by 89 cents. In the afternoon, some who made profits settled their positions, and the prices rose slightly by 1 cent and 5 cents to 2 cents. Outside of the current cotton, foreign merchants are gradually becoming interested. Mumbai Cotton Industry Weekly Report

Japanese merchants purchased Indian cotton in the previous week, which was greatly affected here. This week, Japanese merchants resold, and speculators also engaged in dumping. The condition of new cotton is generally good, except for Central India and the Central Province. The condition of Sindi, Punjab, and Gandhi's flowers is particularly good. Due to the improvement in the weather, Pilar is also improving. Biluo Creek and Goquira are average. Western Kantai has recently benefited from rain. At present, due to high prices, shipments are surging, and they have increased by 57,220 bales compared to the same period last year. Taolela flowers have also increased by 17,234 bales. At the same time, the Japanese exchange rate has plummeted, and import taxes have increased, which are all sufficient to reduce cotton exports. Therefore, cotton inventories have increased greatly compared to last year, and the price difference between India and the United States will also increase. Grain

Pujiang New Early Rice Falls by Half a Yuan

Yesterday, the inland sources in South Shanghai were still plentiful. The accumulation in Pujiang was still thick. The street sales were stagnant due to the modest north market appetite. The price of new early rice still fell by half a yuan. Changxi north early rice, middle pass short triangle, and fresh rice also followed closely. Although there was not much new foreign pointed rice, sales were not smooth, resulting in price adjustments. The early and late rice appetite was still sluggish, and prices were seen to follow the decline.

Yesterday, the river-bottom rice in North Shanghai, Chang Kun Li, and other old and broken rice was more mediocre than before. Affected by the new goods, the opening price was reduced by three corners. The early and late rice in Qingpu and Sisong came from more than a dozen stores, and the transaction was slightly moved to the top quality. The second-quality Jinze goods were stuck, which was quite stagnant and fell by two feet. The Wonton and Rice Cake shops needed a lot of goods, and the situation was slightly tight. New pointed rice was weakly accumulated, and rural sales were stagnant, resulting in weak prices. New early rice fell by half a yuan compared to the South Market.

Saigon Rice Has Qingdao Sales

Yesterday, although the foreign rice had the owners trying to pull up prices, the sales were dull and the market was weak. The appetite of this street turned weak, and the price fell slightly by three to four points. Then, the Qingdao gang went to handle 300 bags of No. 1 Saigon rice. This street also dealt with it slightly, and the market situation began to stabilize. The inventory of Hunan rice has not yet been digested, and the next batch of shipments is still on the way and will arrive in Shanghai soon. However, after arriving in Shanghai, it will be stifled by foreign rice, and the digestion will be even more stagnant. Moreover, the owners are unwilling to sell at a loss due to the high cost. Yesterday, this street handled 100 bags of Jing rice at a price of only 8 yuan, which was half a yuan less than the previous opening price, but it was 78 cents less than the initial opening price at the beginning of last month. The foreign rice opened at 700 small grades at a price of 8 yuan and 9 cents to 8 yuan and 6 cents, and old rice at 8 yuan and 7 and a half cents, and 1,000 bags of No. 1 Saigon rice at a price of 9 yuan and 4 cents to 9 yuan and 3 cents.

Flour Market Feels Slightly Stronger

Yesterday, the flour market generally presented a stable picture. As the foreign wheat quotation continued to improve by about 34 cents, although the transactions in each plate were not very smooth, the overseas sentiment was slightly better due to the improvement of foreign wheat. A portion of the custom helpers also had slight transactions, so the market sentiment was relatively strong. The large and small factories, however, were not very confident in foreign wheat, and were generally waiting and watching without any movement. However, with actual sales not moving forward and the money supply being loose on the surface but tight in reality, it is difficult to expect excitement in the future. The result was that the current month was 5 li larger than the previous week, October was unchanged, November and December were 1 fen larger, January was 1 fen and 2.5 li larger, and February was 1 fen larger.

Future Wheat is Weak in the Near Term and Stable in the Long Term

Yesterday, after the opening of the near-term and far-term wheat markets in the afternoon, each month showed a trend of weakness in the near term and stability in the long term. The near term, such as September and October, was originally stable, but later, due to the fact that the industry had spot goods for sale, the customers were still waiting and watching, because the factories had to calculate before they could have an appetite. The long term was more stable due to the good quotation of foreign wheat, but transactions were rare. As a result, September was 3 fen less than the previous weekend, and October was 4 fen less. The existing wheat remained stable, and the opening price in Yao Bay was 3 taels, 5 cents and 6 fen, with a total of 1,000 bags.

Oil Market

The white wax market is getting worse

The white wax field is a necessity for candle making and red sealing. Since kerosene spirits can be used as substitutes, the sales field has been reduced a lot. In the past, the Guangdong gang also had a large number of sales, but in the past three or four years, it has also been greatly reduced. Recently, the market has not had any major ups and downs, and it has been hovering between 80 and 100 taels throughout the year last year. Since the Shanghai war, the sales field has been even clearer. It could still be maintained in the spring of this year, but it has been declining in the summer and has been unable to recover recently. Half a month ago, the market was still 80 taels, and last week it was 723 taels. According to the Guangdong gang's handling of goods, each batch is only two or three sticks, and there is only one or two batches that can be handled per month, which makes the sales channel even more blocked, and the market is getting worse and worse. It is really not easy to expect it to be good for a while. However, the industry sells rice heart fixed price at 78 taels, and the unified price is 76 taels.

Scholarship and Faculty 75

The decline of scholarship has never been worse than it is today. Speaking of students, many are indulging in a life of extravagance, using books as a disguise and treating the school building as a temporary lodging. Some even excel at sowing discord, colluding with teachers to manipulate fellow students, treating the school as a proving ground for political platforms, and viewing academic pursuits as a stepping stone for advancement. The rest are mediocre and drift with the tide, with few genuinely seeking knowledge or cherishing learning. Speaking of professors, some use teaching hours as a means of making a living, while others regard the school as a temporary stopover. Among colleagues, there is backstabbing, with each establishing their own faction. The interior of a dignified institution of learning is even divided into factions, becoming an open secret. Most heartbreakingly, teachers often exploit students, instigating unrest to eliminate dissenters. Ousting person A today and person B tomorrow, suspending classes and lectures, are seen as commonplace. The conflicts among professors become increasingly fierce, and the surge of student unrest becomes increasingly rampant, to the point of being unmanageable. Therefore, in today's discussion of the decline of scholarship, merely denouncing the arrogance of youth is insufficient to convince students. The moral degradation of teachers is, in fact, a major cause of the decline of scholarship.

In Western countries, the decline of scholarship often occurs in nations where politics is not on the right track. When a nation is fraught with troubles, schools are also fraught with troubles. According to the facts, the rise and fall of politics and scholarship are closely related. However, people often reverse cause and effect, believing that not seeking to improve politics but merely trying to salvage scholarship is a misguided and inferior strategy. They fail to realize that providing sustenance, education, and nurturing is the essence of politics, and that stability and order are merely the foundation of politics. The nation's current urgent needs are indeed stability and order. However, the education provided by schools and the sounds of stringed instruments and singing embody the continuation of the nation's life and the development of the most crucial roots of politics. Abstaining from food for fear of choking is ridiculed by those who understand, yet why do those who solely advocate for salvaging scholarship fail to pay attention to this?

So, what is the way to salvage scholarship? The arrogance of youth is not as deeply entrenched as it seems, but the moral degradation of teachers is the greatest cause of concern. Therefore, if we want to rectify scholarship today, we must first start by rectifying the faculty. Recently, some have said, "Nothing is better than Chinese students, and nothing is worse than Chinese professors." Chinese students are not beyond instruction. If there are good professors who patiently and skillfully guide them, tirelessly and diligently leading students with sincerity and supervising them with strictness, then students will surely be sincerely convinced, the timid will stand up, and the stubborn will be awed. Transforming the declining scholarship into a noble one will be as easy as turning one's hand. If one merely issues repeated orders, using high-handed measures to suppress these emotionally rich youths, without guiding them according to the circumstances to awaken their understanding, then scholarship will become increasingly激烈 and will inevitably lead to an uncontrollable situation, the cessation of music and singing, the closure of schools, the bankruptcy of education, and the ruin of the youths' futures.

The crux of student unrest is not only the lack of qualified teachers, and rectifying the faculty is only one way to salvage scholarship. Moreover, after schools become embroiled in political whirlpools and the economy is affected by the poverty of the national treasury, those running the schools face obstacles everywhere, and maintaining the status quo is already difficult. With such a demoralized spirit, how can they be entrusted with the important task of rectifying scholarship? However, "the transformation of customs depends on the inclinations of a few individuals." If the leaders of academic institutions can be steadfast and unyielding, upholding a spirit of fearless struggle, sharing the joys and sorrows of teachers and students, and daily arousing students with the dangers facing the nation and the people, while also encouraging students to rebuild the nation, then outstanding youths will surely rise up in response. German scholar Fichte's lectures to save the nation are admired by later generations. After the Franco-Prussian War, the Paris School of Political Science acknowledged the shame and cultivated education, as historians have noted. In this time of national crisis, it is precisely the moment for leaders of our academic institutions to demonstrate their capabilities.
